Jamison Brereton

68 (509)
Indra and Varun╠гa
Bharadv─Бja B─Бrhaspatya
11 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh, except jagat─л 9тАУ10
The theme of ritual reciprocity dominates here, with praise of the two dedi cands fairly spare, whether individual or joint. The message is simple: the piously performed sacrifice that we offer to the two gods should be generously rewarded with wealth.
The sacrifice is announced in the first verse, as an enticement to bring the two gods here. The praise, such as it is, comes in the next three verses, a series of super latives characterizing them both in verse 2, a contrastive glance at their respective functions in the second half of verse 3, and an assertion that the two are preeminent even among the other gods in verse 4. (Verse 4 is also noteworthy for the gendered description of the gods; female deities are not usually given recognition when the gods in general are mentioned.)
Wealth is the target of the middle verses (5тАУ8), wealth for priests and patrons alike. The word ray├н тАЬwealthтАЭ is prominent in all four verses.
The final verses (9тАУ11) depict the here-and-now of the sacrifice, happening in real time, as it were, signaled by an occurrence of a form of the annunciatory near-deictic pronoun (тАЬhere is/this hereтАЭ) in each verse (aya╠Бm 9c, ima╠Бm 10a, ida╠Бm 11c). The gods are present at our sacrifice and urged to drink the soma formally announced to them.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Indra and Varuс╣Зa Pace Oldenberg, I do not think this consists of two (much less three) hymns, with 1-8 forming one, 9-11, or 9, 10-11, one or two more. As indicated in the published introduction, the last three vss. focus on the ritual here-and-now, but this topic-switch from praise and request to ritual exhortation is easily accommodated within the same hymn. That 9- 10 are in Jagat─л in contrast to the Triс╣гс╣нubh in the rest of the hymn is not sufficient to signal a hymn break, esp. since 9-10 doesnтАЩt match either of OldenbergтАЩs suggested groupings.

рдорд╣реЗ рдордВрд╣рдиреАрдпреМ рд╣реЗ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╛рд╡рд░реБрдгреМ рд╡рд╛рдВ рдпреБрд╡рдпреЛрд░рд░реНрдереЗ рд╢реНрд░реБрд╖реНрдЯреА рдХреНрд╖рд┐рдкреНрд░рдГ ред рддрдерд╛ рдЪ рдпрд╛рд╕реНрдХрдГ - рд╢реНрд░реБрд╖реНрдЯреАрддрд┐ рдХреНрд╖рд┐рдкреНрд░рдирд╛рдорд╛рд╢реБ рдЕрд╖реНрдЯреАрддрд┐ ’ (рдирд┐рд░реБ. рем. резреи)ред рдпрдЬреНрдЮрдГ рд╕реЛрдордГ рд╕рдЬреЛрд╖рд╛рдГ рдЛрддреНрд╡рд┐рдЧреНрднрд┐рдГ рд╕рд╣рд┐рддрдГ рдЕрджреНрдп рдЖ рд╕рдордиреНрддрд╛рддреН рдЙрджреНрдпрддрдГ рдкреНрд░рд╡реГрддреНрддрдГ ред рдпрдГ рд╕реЛрдордГ рдордиреБрд╖реНрд╡рддреН рдордиреЛрд░рд┐рд╡ рд╡реГрдХреНрддрдмрд░реНрд╣рд┐рд╖рдГ рд╕реНрддреАрд░реНрдгрдмрд░реНрд╣рд┐рд╖рдГ рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирд╕реНрдп рдЗрд╖реЗ рдЕрдиреНрдирд╛рд░реНрдердВ рдорд╣реЗ рдорд╣рддреЗ рд╕реБрдореНрдирд╛рдп рд╕реБрдЦрд╛рдп рдЪ рдпрдЬрдзреНрдпреИ рдпрд╖реНрдЯреБрдВ рд╡рд╛рдореН рдЖрд╡рд╡рд░реНрддрдд рдЖрд╡рд░реНрддрдпрддрд┐ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMighty Indra and Varuс╣Зa, promptly has the Soma returned, engaged conscientiously (with the priests) to offer sacrifice to you to obtain food for him by whom, like Manu, the sacred grass has been clipped; he who (invited you hither) today for exceeding happiness.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The sacrifice has been raised up in concert with obedience, for the man who has twisted the ritual grass to perform sacrifice to you two, as
Manu (did)тАФ
(the sacrifice) that will turn Indra and Varuс╣Зa here today for great
refreshment and for great favor.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Acdg. to Renou, k├бrman- is esp. associated with Indra, ├нс╣г- with Viс╣гс╣Зu, but I see no clear evidence of this.

p─Бr├б- тАШfar shoreтАЩ and p─Бr├бya- тАШcause to cross [to the far shore]тАЩ are of course etymologically related, and here they express allied notions: just as we cause Indra and Viс╣гс╣Зu to reach the тАШfar shoreтАЩ of their labor, so do they cause us to cross something unspecified, but quite possibly the reference is to completing the ritual.

Griffith

HIS honouring rite whose grass is trimmed is offered swiftly to you, in Manu’s wise, accordant,
The rite which Indra-Varuna shall carry this day to high success and glorious issue.

Geldner

Euch beiden vereint ist das Opfer dargebracht worden, dem Wort dessen gehorsam, der wie Manu das Barhis ausgelegt hat, um zu opfern, das Opfer, das heute Indra und Varuna zum Genu├Я, zu gro├Яem Wohlgefallen, zu gro├Яem herbringen soll.

Grassmann

Euch ist zu weihn des Streubereiters Opfer, das mit Erfolg nach Manus Art gereicht wird, Das heut zur Labung Varuna und Indra zu grosser Gunst herwenden mag, die grossen.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou two are the principal (divinities) at the worship of the gods; the distributors of wealth; the most vigorous of heroes; the most liberal among the opulent; possessed of vast strength; destroyers of foes by truth; entire hosts (of yourselves).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

For you two are the most glorious among the gods with your thrusting, and you two are the mightiest of mighty warriors,
the most bountiful of bountiful benefactors, powerfully forceful, fully armed, overcoming obstacles by truth.

Jamison Brereton Notes

It is striking – and perhaps a little insulting – to refer to the gods Indra and Viс╣гс╣Зu as soma-holding tubs, though of course once they have drunk the soma, that is what, in effect, they are. This image recurs in 6d.

The two heavy pres. passive participles ┼Ыasy├бm─Бn─Бс╕е and g─лy├бm─Бn─Бsaс╕е seem meant to convey that the sacrifice is currently ongoing, hence my тАЬas they are being тАжтАЭ In d arka├нс╕е is taken by Geldner and Renou as referring to the chants of the sacrifice, and in the context of recitation and singing this sense is clearly the principal one. Both Geldner and Renou interpr. the instr. as meaning тАЬin the form of,тАЭ and I have followed them in the published translation – though an instr. of accompaniment тАЬalong with chantsтАЭ would also be possible. I further think the word is a pun, with the secondary sense тАЬalong with the rays (of the sun)тАЭ as often (e.g., VI.4.6). This would be a temporal designation of dawn, when the sacrifice is taking place. That the next vs. contains a similar pun (in my view) supports such an interpr. here.

Griffith

For at Gods’ worship they are best through vigour; they have become the strongest of the Heroes;
With mighty strength, most liberal of the Princes, Chiefs of the host, by Law made Vrtra’s slayers.

Geldner

Denn ihr beide seid die Ersten in der G├╢tterschaft an Eifer, denn ihr seid die Tapfersten unter den Tapferen, die Freigebigsten unter den Freigebigen, die Mutvollen, die durch das Gesetz mit voller Wehr die Feinde ├╝berwinden.

Grassmann

Denn ihr ja seid die eifrigsten der G├╢tter, die st├дrksten seid ihr unter starken Helden, Sehr kr├дftige, der Geber gabenreichste, mit ganzer Schar in Wahrheit Feindbezwinger.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬPraise Mitra and Varuс╣Зa, renowned or all glorious energies and enjoyment; one of whom slays Vс╣Ыtra with the thunderbolt, the other, intelligent by his might, comes to the aid (of the pious when) in difficulties.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

By reason of their favors, sing to Indra and Varuс╣Зa, who take delight, with forceful, reverential (songs).
The one smites Vr╠еtra with his might and mace; the other as inspired poet attends upon the (ritual) enclosures.

Jamison Brereton Notes

dr├бviс╣Зo d├бdh─Бn─Б in b is essentially the same VP as dr├бviс╣Зam тАж dhattam in 1c. I do not know why the s-stem dr├бvinas- was substituted for the thematic dr├бviс╣Зa-, esp. as the acc. of the latter, dr├бviс╣Зam, would fit the meter just as well. The first VP, dr├бviс╣Зaс╣Г dhattam, reappears in 6c.

There are other echoes of previous vss.: 3cd s├бс╣Г v─Бm тАж s├бm repeats 1a, and mat─лn─Б╠Бm in c both repeats the same word in the same metrical position in 2a and anticipates it in 4c.

The 2nd half of this vs. is structured like that of vs. 2, esp. p─Бda d, where both 2d and 3d have the form PREV st├│m─Бsaс╕е PRES.PASS.PART. INSTR.(тАШsongтАЩ)-aiс╕е. The instr.

could, as in the previous vs., express accompaniment.

As in 2, I see a pun here: because of the etym. figure a├▒jantv akt├║bhiс╕е тАЬlet them anoint with ointments,тАЭ the principal sense of akt├║- must be тАШointmentтАЩ, here metaphorical for the тАЬointments of thoughts.тАЭ But instr. akt├║bhiс╕е often means тАШthrough the nightsтАЩ, as in the phrase dy├║bhir akt├║bhiс╕е тАЬthrough the days and the nightsтАЭ (e.g., I.112.25), and I see this temporal sense here as well.

Griffith

Praise those Twain Gods for powers that merit worship, Indra and Varuna, for bliss, the joyous.
One with his might and thunderbolt slays Vrtra; the other as a Sage stands near in troubles.

Lobe die beiden mit ehrf├╝rchtigen Aufmunterungen, Indra und Varuna, die wegen ihrer Gunsterweisung begehrt sind. Der eine schl├дgt mit der Keule kraftvoll den Vritra, der andere ist im Bunde der G├╢tter als Weisheitsk├╝nder zugegen.

Grassmann

Sie preise nun mit ehrfurchtsvollen Liedern, die sang-erfreuten Varuna und Indra; Der eine schl├дgt mit Blitz und Kraft den Vritra, der andre hilft als weiser in Gemeinden.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬWhen among mankind, both males and feminine les, and when all the gods spontaneously striving glorify you, Indra and Varuс╣Зa, you become pre-eminent in greatness over them, as do you, wide heaven and earth (surpass them also).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

When all the gods, both ladies and men, grow strong, (their praises) sung for their own sake by (our) men,
you stand out from them by your greatness, o Indra and Varuс╣Зa, (and also you two) wide ones, o Heaven and Earth.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As just noted, mat─л╠Бn─Бm occurs here for the 3rd time, while juс╣г├йth─Бm is repeated from 1c.

Griffith

Though dames and men have waxen strong and mighty, and all the Gods selfpraised among the Heroes,
Ye, Indra-Varuna, have in might surpassed them, and thus were ye spread wide, O Earth and Heaven.

Geldner

Als alle G├╢tter - Frauen und M├дnner - die sich selbst Lobenden unter den M├дnnern, stark wurden, da waret ihr beide, Indra und Varuna, ihnen an Gr├╢├Яe voraus, und ihr beide, Himmel und Erde, die weiten.

Grassmann

Wenn alle G├╢tter, Weiber auch und M├дnner, sich m├дchtig zeigen, hochgelobt von S├дngern, Seid ihr voran doch, Varuna und Indra, wie Himmel gross und wie die weite Erde.

English translation:

тАЬHe who spontaneously presents you, Indra and Varuс╣Зa (oblations), is liberal, wealthy and upright; he has to prosper with the food of his adversary, and possess riches, and opulent descendants.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Just he acquires good gifts and good help and possesses the truth who ritually serves you, o Indra and Varuс╣Зa, in his own person.
With refreshment he, possessing gifts, could overcome hostilities; he will gain wealth and wealthy peoples.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As noted in the published introduction, both gods are credited with wide striding (b), although this is normally only Viс╣гс╣ЗuтАЩs act. The cosmogonic opening out of the spaces in the more vaguely phrased 2nd hemistich can be applied to Indra, however.

Griffith

Righteous is he, and liberal and helpful who, Indra-Varuna, brings you gifts with gladness.
That bounteous man through food shall conquer faemen, and win him opulence and wealthy people.

Geldner

Nur der ist reich an Gaben und Gunst, ist rechtschaffen, wer gegen euch, Indra und Varuna, von selbst opferwillig ist. Der Freigebige soll an Speisesegen seine Feinde ├╝berbieten; er soll Reichtum und die reichen Leute f├╝r sich gewinnen.

Grassmann

Der ist gerecht, an Gaben reich und Beistand, der Indra euch und Varuna verehret; Mit Kraft begabt wird er die Feinde schlagen, erlangen Gut und g├╝terreiche Leute.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay that opulence comprising treasure and abundant food, which you besow, deities, upon the donor (of the oblation), that, Indra and Varuс╣Зa, which baffles the calumnies of the malevolent, be ours.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The wealth that you two provide to the man who performs pious ceremoniesтАФwealth consisting of goods and much livestockтАФ
may that abide in us, o Indra and Varuс╣ЗaтАФ(the wealth) that shatters the taunts of the rapacious ones.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The image of the gods as soma-holding tubs returns here in d, but this time it is mediated through the image of them as the sea (samudr├бс╕е) and therefore couched in the singular.

The d p─Бda is a repetition of 4d, save for the substitution of h├бvam for g├нraс╕е.

Such verbatim repetition of a full p─Бda within a hymn is very rare (save for refrains) and relatively rare even between two hymn – again, in my view, an indication that the poet was not feeling particularly inspired.

Griffith

May wealth which ye bestow in food and treasure on him who brings you gifts and sacrifices,
Wealth, Gods! which breaks the curse of those who vex us, be, Indra-Varuna, e’en our own possession.

Geldner

Uns soll der Reichtum zufallen, Indra und Varuna, den ihr beiden G├╢tter dem Opferspender bringet, aus Gut und viel Vieh bestehend, der die Hohnreden der Neider bricht.

Grassmann

Das Gut, das ihr dem frommen Opfrer schenket, das reich an Schatz und Nahrung ist, ihr G├╢tter, Das wohn’ uns bei, o Varuna und Indra, das schnell zerbricht den Fluch und Spott der Feinde.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬMay that opulence, Indra and Varuс╣Зa, which is a sure defence, and of which the gods are the guardians, be ours, celebrating our praise, whose destroying prowess in battles victorious (over foes) speedily obscures (their) fame.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

And, o Indra and Varuс╣Зa, for our patrons may there be wealth offering good protection, with gods as its herdsmenтАФ

(our patrons) whose impetuous force, victorious in battles, surpassingly extends their e╠Бclat all at once.

Jamison Brereton Notes

In ab Geldner honors the p─Бda break and construes s├│masya with jaс╣нh├бram pс╣Ыс╣Зeth─Бm. But we might expect an instr. s├│mena in that case (as in V.34.2), and the enjambment envisioned here is very mild.

Griffith

So also, Indra-Varuna, may our princes have riches swift to save, with Gods to guard them-
They whose great might gives victory in battles, and their triumphant glory spreads with swiftness.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬDivine and glorified Indra and Varuс╣Зa, quickly bestow upon us wealth for our felicity; and thus eulogising he strength of you two, mighty (deities), may we pass over all difficulties as (we cross) the waters with a boat.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Now, Indra and Varuс╣Зa, as you are being sung, replenish our wealth for the excellence of our fame, o gods.
In just this way singing the force of the great one, might we cross over difficulties, as if over waters by boat.

Jamison Brereton Notes

On the surprise ending here and the splitting up of what was throughout the rest of the hymn an indissoluble pair, see published introduction. The first p─Бda keeps the two as a pair, with dual verbs jigyathuс╕е and jayethe asserting that both won and both did not lose the contest. The audience would first take this as meaning they did not lose to their (joint) opponent. But in b we have the first splitting of the pair into two (implied) singulars (n├б тАж katar├бs cana├нnoс╕е тАЬneither one of these twoтАЭ), which could raise the possibility that they were contending with each other – but paradoxically neither one lost. Their mutual contention is then made explicit in p─Бda c, with, inter alia, a reverse V─Бyav Indra┼Ы ca construction (├нndra┼Ы ca viс╣гс╣Зo) serving as the subj. of a dual verb (├бpasс╣Ыdheth─Бm), which in the middle voice refers to mutual conflict, and the final p─Бda explains (or implies) how in such a situation neither one lost: the 1000 (cows) were split into three parts, and as later Vedic texts indicate, Indra got twothirds and Viс╣гс╣Зu one-third. It may be that the reversal of the V─Бyav Indra┼Ы ca construction, which puts ├нndraс╕е in first position, also signals his relative, but not complete, dominance in this story.

Griffith

Indra. and Varuna, Gods whom we are lauding, mingle ye wealth with our heroic glory.
May we, who praise the strength of what is mighty, pass dangers, as with boats we cross the waters.

Geldner

So mehret denn gepriesen, o Indra und Varuna, ihr G├╢tter, unseren Reichtum, da├Я wir in Guten Ruf kommen! Also die St├дrke des M├дchtigen lobpreisend, m├╢chten wir ├╝ber die F├дhrlichkeiten hin├╝berkommen wie zu Schiff ├╝ber ein Gew├дsser.

Grassmann

Nun f├╝llt, gepriesne, Varuna und Indra, uns Reichthum zu zum Wohlergehn, o G├╢tter; In Wahrheit preisend des gewalt’gen St├дrke, durchfahren Noth wir, wie den Strom im Schiffe.

Elizarenkova

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ (рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╛рд╡рд░реБрдгрд╛) рд╕реВрд░реНрдп рдФрд░ рдЪрдиреНрджреНрд░рдорд╛ рдХреЗ рддреБрд▓реНрдп рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдорд╛рди (рдирдГ) рд╣рдо рд▓реЛрдЧреЛрдВ рдХреЛ (рдЧреГрдгрд╛рдирд╛) рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рд╛ рдХрд░рдиреЗ рдФрд░ (рджреЗрд╡рд╛) рджреЗрдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рд░рд╛рдЬрдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдЬрдиреЛ ! рдЬреИрд╕реЗ рддреБрдо рджреЛрдиреЛрдВ (рд╕реМрд╢реНрд░рд╡рд╕рд╛рдп) рдЙрддреНрддрдо рдпрд╢ рд╣реЛрдиреЗ рдХреЗ рд▓рд┐рдпреЗ (рд░рдпрд┐рдореН) рдзрди рдХрд╛ (рдкреГрдЩреНрдХреНрддрдореН) рд╕рдореНрдмрдиреНрдз рдХрд░реЛ (рдЗрддреНрдерд╛) рдРрд╕реЗ (рдорд╣рд┐рдирд╕реНрдп) рдмреЬреЗ рдХреЗ (рд╢рд░реНрдзрдГ) рдмрд▓ рдХреА (рдЧреГрдгрдиреНрддрдГ) рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рд╛ рдХрд░рддреЗ рд╣реБрдП рд╣рдо рд▓реЛрдЧ (рдирд╛рд╡рд╛) рдирд╛рд╡ рд╕реЗ (рдЕрдкрдГ) рдЬрд▓реЛрдВ рдХреЛ (рди) рдЬреИрд╕реЗ рд╡реИрд╕реЗ (рджреБрд░рд┐рддрд╛) рджреБрдГрдЦ рд╕реЗ рдЙрд▓реНрд▓рдЩреНрдШрди рдХрд░рдиреЗ рдпреЛрдЧреНрдп рдХрд╖реНрдЯреЛрдВ рдХреЛ (рдиреВ) рд╢реАрдШреНрд░ (рддрд░реЗрдо) рддрд░реЗрдВ реереорее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬRepeat acceptable and all-comprehensive praise to the imperial mighty divine Varuс╣Зa, he who, endowed with greatness, with wisdom, and with splendour, illumines the spacious (heaven and earth).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Now chant forth at length your own dear thought to the lofty sovereign king, to the god Varuс╣Зa.
Here is the one of great commandments who radiates through the two wide (worlds) with his greatness and by his resolve, like unaging (fire) with its flame.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner also (n. 8c) claims (fld. by Renou) that this vs. is entirely Varuс╣ЗaтАЩs. This is more plausible: he is mentioned by name in b, and m├бhivrataс╕е тАШhaving great commandmentsтАЩin c makes it likely that the clause in cd has Varuс╣Зa as subject тАФ though note that m├бhivrata- is used of Varuс╣Зa only here, with two occurrences each of Agni and Soma, and moreover dhс╣Ыtavrat─Б is addressed to both gods in the next vs. (10b). Nonetheless, samr─Б╠Бj- in p─Бda a is used frequently of Indra as well as of Varuс╣Зa, so the 1st hemistich may (and probably does) contain a exhortation to the poet to chant both to Indra (as sovereign king) and Varuс╣Зa. The published translation could make this clearer if тАШandтАЩ replaced the comma: тАЬto the lofty sovereign king (and) to the god Varuс╣ЗaтАЭ

Jamison Brereton Notes

On the annunciatory forms of ay├бm in these three vss., see published introduction.

Griffith

Now will I sing a dear and far-extending hymn to Varuna the God, sublime, imperial Lord,
Who, mighty Governor, Eternal, as with flame, illumines both wide worlds with majesty and power.

Geldner

Stimme dem hohen Allherrscher ein angenehmes Lied an, dem Gott Varuna ein umf├дngliches! Er ist es, der die beiden weiten Himmel und Erde mit seiner Einsicht erleuchtet wie der alterlose Agni mit seiner Glut, er, der mit Macht m├дchtig Gebietende.

Grassmann

Auf, singe nun ein Lied dem hohen Opferherrn, ein liebes, grosses ihm, dem Gotte Varuna, dem m├дcht’gen Herrscher, der mit Macht das Weltenpaar voll Kraft durchstrahlt, mit Licht wie der, der nie verlischt.

Elizarenkova

тАЬIndra and Varuс╣Зa, observant of holy duties, drinkers of the Soma, drink this exhilarating effused libation; your chariot approaches along the road to the sacrifice, (that you may partake) of the food of the gods and drink (the Soma).тАЭ

Griffith

True to Law, Indra-Varuna, drinkers of the juice, drink this pressed Soma which shall give you rapturous joy.
Your chariot cometh to the banquet of the Gods, to sacrifice, as it were home, that ye may drink.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬDrink, Indra and Varuс╣Зa, showerers (of benefits), of the most sweet Soma, the shedder (of blessings); this your Soma, is poured forth by us; sitting on the sacred grass, be exhilarated (by the draught).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

O Indra and Varuс╣Зa, you bullsтАФdrench yourselves in the most
honeyed, bullish soma.
This stalk has been poured all around for you here among us. Having sat down on this ritual grass, bring yourselves to exhilaration.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The 2nd p─Бda has a rather insistent but elementary phonetic/etymological figure: vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гс╣Зaс╕е тАж vс╣Ыс╣гan─Б╠Бvс╣Ыс╣гeth─Бm, and the last word of the vs. m─Бdayeth─Бm resonates with the long adj. qualifying soma in the 1st p─Бda, m├бdhumattamasya. ## 069 Indra and Viс╣гс╣Зu RenouтАЩs treatment is in EVP XV.43-46. He claims that the тАЬth├иme indraiqueтАЭ dominates, though I find the hymnтАЩs phraseology so bland that itтАЩs difficult to assign qualities and deeds to one or the other, and in fact the most salient action in the hymn, the wide-striding of vs. 5, is Viс╣гс╣ЗuтАЩs characteristic deed. See further in the published introduction.

The hymn is (in my view) repetitive and pedestrian, with only a few striking images and phraseological tricks. This strikes me as an indication that the poet was тАЬphoning it inтАЭ – the composition of the hymn does not seem to have commanded his full attention. The question might then arise why the hymn was preserved in the Saс╣Гhit─Б. This might be partially due to the rarity of Indra-Viс╣гс╣Зu hymns (only the first three vss. of I.155 and the middle three vss. of VII.99 – so this is the only hymn entirely dedicated to both) and in fact of Viс╣гс╣Зu hymns in general. As Viс╣гс╣Зu, a fairly recessive god in the RV, began to come to prominence in the post-RVic period, the assemblers of the RV collection may have gathered what scraps they could and exercised less critical judgment than usual in order to create a place in the text for this newly important deity. The OтАЩHenry-type ending, sprung by the final vs. (8), might also account for its preservation.

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдпрд╛ рдордВрддреНрд░рд╛рдд рд╡рд╛рдЪрдХрд▓реБрдкреНрддреЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдВрдХрд╛рд░ рдЖрд╣реЗ. рдЬреЗ рд╕реЛрдорд▓рддрд╛ рдЗрддреНрдпрд╛рджреА рд░рд╕рдпреБрдХреНрдд рдЕрдиреНрдирдкрд╛рди рдХрд░реВрди рд╕реНрд╡рддрдГ рдЖрдирдВрджрд┐рдд рд╣реЛрдКрди рдЖрдореНрд╣рд╛рд▓рд╛ рдЖрдирдВрджрд┐рдд рдХрд░рддрд╛рдд рддреНрдпрд╛рдВрдЪрд╛рдЪ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рдВрдиреА рд╕рддреНрдХрд╛рд░ рдХрд░рд╛рд╡рд╛. рее резрез рее
